+Jamison Brereton

20 (640)
Maruts
Sobhar─л K─Бс╣Зva
26 verses: kakubh alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, arranged in prag─Бthas
The typical Marut themes are deftly woven together in this hymn. After inviting them to the sacrifice (vss. 1тАУ2), the poet first describes the effects in nature of the storm they embody (vss. 3тАУ6) and then their flashy beauty and that of their chariot (vss. 7тАУ12), ending this section with two verses (13тАУ14) on their lack of individuality (see also vs. 21). The remainder of the hymn concerns the generosity of the Maruts and begs them to display it in response to SobhariтАЩs hymn: the poet addresses him
self in verses 19тАУ20. Unlike the generic gifts generally asked for in R╠еgvedic hymns, the final verses make it clear that the poet has a specific request: Marut medicine to heal the afflicted (vss. 23тАУ26). Their association with healing comes through their father Rudra.
The hymn exhibits a light touch and has a number of neat turns of phraseтАФfor instance, verse 8, where тАЬthe music of the Sobharis is anointed with cowsтАЭ indicates that their hymn reaps a bovine reward from the patron, or verse 19, with its pun on the participle c├бrkr╠ес╣гat meaning both тАЬplowingтАЭ and тАЬcelebrating.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFar-travellig (winds), alike wrathful, come here, harm us not; benders of the solid (mountains), withdrawnot from us.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Come here; donтАЩt mean harm. Setting out, donтАЩt stay away, o you of equal spirit,
who are able to bow even the fixed things.

+Griffith

LET none, Swift Travellers! check you: come hither, like-spirited, stay not far away,
Ye benders even of what is firm.

+Geldner

Kommt, verseht euch nicht, bleibt nicht fern, ihr Ausfahrer, von gleichem Eifer beseelt, die ihr sogar das Feste beuget.

+Grassmann

O kommt herbei und s├дumet nicht, o gleichgesinnte, brechet auf, nicht bleibet fern, Ihr, die ihr auch das Feste beugt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey fall upon the island; the firm-set (trees) are with difficulty sustained; they agitate both heaven andearth; they urge on the waters; bright- weaponed, far-shining, whatever (you approach) you cause to tremble.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

“The islands fall asunder, the firmest (trees) experience distress; they (the winds) distress heaven and earth; thewaters hurry onward, O bright-weaponed, self- shining ones, when you agitate them

+Jamison Brereton

The islands keep flying further apart; misfortune stands still; they [=Maruts] yoke both world-halves.
The wasteplaces rise forth, when you stir (them), o you self-radiant
ones with beautiful bangles.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. describes the effects of the monsoon. The first hemistich contains three injunctives (p─Б╠Бpatan, t├нс╣гс╣нhat, and yujanta) and the last p─Бda a present (├йjatha), but p─Бda c contains the apparently augmented airata. Given this collection of verbs, it is difficult to produce a consistent temporal interpretation. The injunctives can harmonize either with the preterital airata or with the presential ├йjatha, but those two are incompatible. A way out of this dilemma was shown by Hoffmann (Injunc, 210), who suggests that the тАЬcacophonous hiatusтАЭ dh├бnv─Бni *─лrata was avoided by substituting the augmented form for the injunctive. (It would be good to have other exx. of such a hiatus-avoiding technique, however.) The whole verse can then be interpr. as presential or тАЬgeneral.тАЭ This temporal value continues in vs. 5, also describing the effects of the storm, with two present-tense verbs.

The second clause in p─Бda a, t├нс╣гс╣нhad duch├║n─Б, has been interpreted in two opposing senses. Geldner supplies the v├н of the first VP and tr. тАЬdas Unheil breitet sich aus.тАЭ But without the v├н the verb would mean тАШstand (still)тАЩ or тАШstopтАЩ (so Renou тАЬstoppe le mis├иreтАЭ). I favor this latter interpretation. Since the monsoon brings desired rain, which makes the plants grow and produces food and attendant well-being, it stops misery in its tracks, as it were. This stoppage contrasts with the movement of the features of the natural world in p─Бdas a and c.

+Griffith

Islands are bursting forth and misery is stayed: the heaven and earth are joined in one.
Decked with bright rings, ye spread the broad expanses out, when ye, Self. luminous, stirred yourselves.

+Geldner

Die Inseln zerstieben, das Unheil breitet sich aus; sie spannen Himmel und Erde vor. Die Steppen kamen in Bewegung, wenn ihr Sch├╢nberingte euch aufmachet, ihr Selbstgl├дnzende.

+Grassmann

Die Wolkeninseln stoben und das Unheil floh, und Erd’ und Himmel eintet ihr, O Ring-geschm├╝ckte, eure Bogen drangen vor, wenn ihr euch regt, o leuchtende.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton

(When you stir) even the unshakeable things on your drive, the
mountains and the lord of the forest keep resounding.
The earth trembles at your journeys.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There are several ways to treat p─Бda a. The simplest (and to my mind the least satisfactory) is simply to take ├бcyut─Б as another subject of 3rd pl. n─Б╠Бnadati (so, e.g., Schaeffer, Inten.). With Geldner and Renou, an intrans. тАШshakeтАЩ (vel sim.) can be supplied, on the basis of passages like VI.31.2b ├бcyut─Б cic cy─Бvayanta r├бj─Бс╣Гsi, whose d-p─Бda ends ├бjman ─Б╠Бte, very like this p─Бda. I favor a different solution: simply continuing y├бd ├йjatha тАЬwhen you stirтАЭ from the preceding p─Бda (4d). Although the two verses do not belong to the same prag─Бtha, the continuity of theme is clear.

тАЬ(Alarmed) at your violence, Maruts, the heaven seeks to rise higher, abandoning the firmament, where(you) the strong-armed leaders (of rites) display the ornaments of (your) person ns.тАЭ

To allow your onslaught to drive by, o Maruts, heaven raises itself higher aloft,
when the men, strong in arm, keep putting their energies on display on their own bodies.

I read ├бnu both with what precedes (svadh─Б╠Бm) and what follows (┼Ыr├нyam) and do not, contra Geldner, take the latter as obj. of v├бhante. Med. forms of v├бha- are several times used reflexively of the MarutsтАЩ progress (V.58.1, V.60.7, V.61.11, X.77.6) without obj.

My tr. of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-psu- and ├бhruta-psu- (as well as vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-psu- in 10a) are owing to Thieme. See reff. at comm. ad I.49.3.

рд╕реЛрднрд░реАрдгрд╛рдореН рдЛрд╖реАрдгрд╛рдВ рдЧреЛрднрд┐рдГ рд╢рдмреНрджреИрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреИрдГ рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдорд░реБрджреНрд╡реАрдгрд╛ рдЕрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ рд╡реНрдпрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯреАрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗред рдХреБрддреНрд░ред рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрдпреЗ рд░рдереЗ рдХреЛрд╢реЗ рдХреЛрд╢рд╡рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддреЗ рдордзреНрдпрджреЗрд╢реЗред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЧреЛрднрд┐рд░реНрдЧрдиреНрддреГрднрд┐рд░реНрдЧреЛрдорд╛рддреГрдХреИрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгреЛрд╜рдЬреНрдпрддреЗ рд╡реНрдпрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реЛрднрд░реАрдгрд╛рдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдпреЗрджреГрд╢реЗ рд░рдереЗ рд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдЧреЛрдмрдиреНрдзрд╡рдГ рдЧреЛрдорд╛рддреГрдХрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╕рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдЬрдиреНрдорд╛рдирдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреБрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЗрд╖реЗ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдп рднреБрдЬреЗ рднреЛрдЧрд╛рдп рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░реАрддреНрдпреИ рдЪ рдмрд▓рдирд╛рдп рд╡рд╛ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рднрд╡рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe voice (of the Maruts) blends with the songs of the Sobharis in the receptacle of their goldenchariot; may the mighty well-born Maruts, the offspring of the (bridled) cow, (be gracious) to us regard of food,enjoyment, and kindness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The voice: v─Бс╣Зa = the lute, v─лс╣З─Б

+Jamison Brereton

The music of the Sobharis is anointed with cows. Onto the chariot, into the golden (chariot) cask
(come) those well-born (Maruts), akin to a cow [=Pr╠е┼Ыni], (for us) to
enjoy nourishment; the great ones (come here) now for us to gain.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Against most tr., I take p─Бda a as an independent nominal clause and construe b with c. The locc. in b refer to the chariot and its box, onto which the Maruts are mounting. The same phrase two hymns later, VIII.22.9 ─Б╠Бh├н ruh├бtam тАж, r├бthe k├│┼Ыe hiraс╣Зy├бye, with a verb of mounting, seems to clinch this interpr., though Geldner (n. 8b) explicitly claims that the two nearby phrases, in hymns by the same poet, are used differently.

I think g├│-bandhu- тАШhaving a cow/cows as kinтАЩ is a pun, an interpr. not registered in the published translation On the one hand it refers to the MarutsтАЩ mother Pс╣Ы┼Ыni; on the other, on the basis of v─Б╠Бja-bandhu- тАШhaving prizes as kinтАЩ (VIII.68.19) and the word play in the adjacent hymn, VIII.21.4 (see comm. there), it is also a clever way to say that the Maruts have cows at their disposal to give to us. These are the same cows with which the music is anointed in p─Бda a.

I do not see any way around supplying a verb of motion or mounting in bcd: the Maruts mount their chariot or come in order for us to enjoy the nourishment they bring (cf. 2c iс╣г─Б╠Бnah тАж ─Б╠Бgat─Б тАЬcome here to us with nourishmentтАЭ) and to gain other desirable things, in two parallel infinitive phrases (iс╣г├й bhuj├й тАж na sp├бrase).

The root noun ├нс╣г- is tr. two different ways in 2c (тАШrefreshmentтАЩ) and 8c (тАШnourishmentтАЩ). These should have been harmonized.

+Griffith

The pivot of the Sobharis’ chariot within the golden box is balmed with milk.
May they the Well-born, Mighty, kindred of the Cow, aid us to food and to delight.

+Geldner

Mit Kuhmilch wird die Stimme der Sobhari┬┤s gesalbt in der goldenen Kufe auf dem Wagen. Die mit der Kuh, der Prisni, verwandten, edlen Marut, die gro├Яen, m├╢gen uns Speisesegen genie├Яen und davontragen lassen.

+Grassmann

Durch Milchtrank wird der Sobhari’s Musik belohnt, den ihr im goldnen Wagen f├╝hrt, Ihr sch├╢ngebornen, kuhentstammten, m├дchtigen, verhelft zu Trunk uns und Genuss.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSprinklers of the libation, present the offerings to the rain-bestowing swift-passing company of theMaruts.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O you who rain unguents, present oblations to your own bullish Marutian troop
whose leader is a bull [=Indra].

+Griffith

Bring, ye who sprinkle balmy drops. oblations to your vigorous Marut company,
To those whose leader is the Bull.

+Geldner

Bringet, ihr Salbetriefende, eure Opfergaben der bullenhaften marutischen Heerschar dar, deren Anf├╝hrer der Bulle Indra ist.

+Grassmann

Auf bringt, o Salben-regnende, nun eurer starken Marutschar die Opfer dar, ihr, der mit Stieren fahrenden.

+Elizarenkova

тАЬMaruts, leaders (of rites), come like swift-flying birds in your rain- shedding, strong-horsed chariot,whose wheels bestow showers, to partake of our oblations.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

come here at will, like winged falcons, to pursue our oblations, o men.

Lightly like winged falcons, O ye Heroes, come, come to enjoy our ofrerings.

+Grassmann

Mit stierbespanntem Wagen kommt, o Maruts, her, der stark an Naben, stark sich zeigt, O M├дnner kommt wie Adler fliegend schnell daher, zu speisen unser Opfermahl.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFierce, vigorous, strong-armed, they need not exert (the energy of their) person ns; bows and arrows areready in your chariots; the glory (of conquest) over (hostile) armies is yours.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Energy: or, rather, they need notexert themselves to defend their person ns, nakiс╣гс╣нan┼лс╣гu yetire

+Jamison Brereton

These mighty bulls with mighty arms do not arrange (such things just) on their bodies:
taut bows and weapons are on your chariots, beauties on your faces.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes tan┼л╠Бс╣гu as attenuated to something close to a reflexive (тАЬsind nicht auf sich selbst eifers├╝chitigтАЭ), but in vss. 6 and 26 it is lexically robust. I think the point here is to contrast the adornment of their bodies with that of other locations associated with them (their chariots and their faces).

+Griffith

They toil not to defend their bodies from attack, strong Heroes with their mighty arms.
Strong are your bows and strong the weapons in your cars, and glory sits on every face.

+Geldner

Die gewaltigen Bullen mit gewaltigen Armen sind nicht auf sich selbst eifers├╝chtig. Starke Bogen und Waffen sind auf euren Wagen, Sch├╢nheit in euren Gesichtern.

+Grassmann

Die kr├дft’gen Helden, deren Arme kr├дftig sind, sie hadern miteinander nie, Auf ihren Wagen starke Bogen, Kriegsger├дth und Glanz auf ihrem Angesicht.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬOne illustrious name is given to them all, as widely diffused as water for the gratification (of theirworshippers), like invigoraing paternal food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vayo na pitryam sahaс╕е: prasahana┼Ы─лlam; the worshipers may relyupon it

+Jamison Brereton

Of them whose name is vibrant and widespread like a flood, there is just one (name) for each and every one of them to enjoy.
Their might is like the life force of their fathers.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

That their name can be тАЬbroad/widespread like a floodтАЭ may at first seem odd, but the point is simply that it is widely known.

P─Бda b expresses another common point about the Maruts: they do not have individual names (though see V.52.10-11), but тАЬMarutтАЭ serves for each one of them.

I differ from Geldner and Renou in taking gen. pl. ┼Ы├б┼Ыvat─Бm тАШof each and every oneтАЩ as referring to the Maruts, not to the mass of people; therefore in my view the subj. of the inf. bhuj├й is the Maruts, not these same unidentified people.

I do not know if p├нtrya- here refers specifically to the MarutsтАЩ ancestors (esp., presumably, Rudra), as I have taken it, or whether this is a more general statement: тАЬlike ancestral life forceтАЭ (so, more or less, Geldner and Renou).

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPraise them, praise the Maruts, for we are (dependen) upon those agitators (of all things) as a menial isupon his lords; therefore are their donations (characterized) by munificence; such are their (gifts).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Extol these Maruts; praise them. For of these boisterous ones, as of wheel-spokes, there is no last one. This is so as to their giving; as to their greatness is this so.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg points out (and as is reflected in GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs tr.), n├б must stand for *n├б n├б, i.e., the simile marker followed by a negative. The same no-last-spoke image is found in V.58.5 with alternative realizations of both simile marker (iva) and negative (privative a-): ar─Б╠Бiv├йd ├бcaram─Б(с╕е).

The p─Бda break between c and d goes counter to the syntactic parallelism: syntax: t├бd eс╣г─Бm d─Бn─Б╠Б meter: … t├бd eс╣г─Бm, mahn─Б╠Бt├бd eс╣г─Бm d─Бn─Б╠Бmahn─Б╠Бt├бd eс╣г─Бm This produces a syncopated effect, emphasized by the polarized positions of the parallel instr. d─Бn─Б╠Бand mahn─Б╠Бin their nominal clauses.

+Griffith

Pay honour to these Maruts and sing praise to them, for of the wheel-spokes of the car
Of these loud roarers none is last: this is their power, this moves them to give mighty gifts.

+Geldner

Diese Marut lobe, diese preise, denn von den Rauschenden gibt es wie bei den Radspeichen keinen Letzten! Das gilt von ihrer Freigebigkeit, das von ihrer Gr├╢├Яe.

+Grassmann

Verehre, preise diese Maruts; denn sie sind laut rauschend Rades Speichen gleich, Von denen keine je die letzte ist, so sind auch sie an Gaben und an Macht.

+Elizarenkova

In c the presence of both v─Б тАШorтАЩ and ut├б тАШandтАЩ is curious, as is the position of the latter. Klein (DGRV I.450) suggests that the placement of ut├б after n┼лn├бm means that it should be construed with that adv., and so v─Б and ut├б each retains its own force.

+Jamison Brereton

Or the prize-seeker whose oblations you come here to pursue, o men. He will attain to your favors, you shakers, along with brilliant things and the winning of prizes.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The y├бsya v─Б opening this verse, parallel to y├│ v─Б in 15c, shows that this clause is still dependent on the main clause in 15ab subh├бgaс╕е s├б тАЬvery fortunate he тАжтАЭ The main clause in 16c may refer only to the v─Бj├нn- of ab or to the various subh├бga- folk of vss. 15-16.

The hapax gatha in b is an anomalous form, with a present 2nd pl. ending (- tha) on a root aorist stem. It is clearly a nonce form generated beside 2nd pl. impv.

gata in 10d. The p─Бdas are otherwise almost identical: 10d havy─Б╠Бno v─лt├бye gata, 16b ─Б╠Бhavy─Б╠Бv─лt├бye gatha.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The identity and distribution of forms in p─Бda b are oddly unclear. Is div├бс╕е dependent on ├бsurasya, or are they coreferential, or are they independent of each other? In the first instance this produces тАЬlord of heavenтАЭ (as I have it in the published tr; see also W. E. Hale [Asura, p. 75] тАЬof the asura of the SkyтАЭ); in the 2nd тАЬLord HeavenтАЭ (so Geldner: тАЬAsura HimmelтАЭ); in the 3rd RenouтАЩs тАЬ(les hommes) du ciel, de lтАЩAsura.тАЭ Do these genitives qualify Rudra (gen. rudr├бsya in a), as I take it, or vedh├бsaс╕е (so Geldner: тАЬdie тАж Meister des Asura Himmel,тАЭ sim. W. E. Hale), or, with Renou, are they direct qualifiers of the Maruts? I opt for the first solution because vedh├бsdoes not usually govern anything and because Rudra is called ├бsuro mah├│ div├бс╕е in II.1.6, div├│ ├бsur─Бya in V.41.3, and probably div├бh … ├бsurasya in I.122.1 contra Geldner

And in fact is vedh├бsaс╕е nom. pl., as itтАЩs universally taken, or another gen. sg., perhaps qualifying Rudra? Parallels cut both ways. Rudra is in fact called vedh├бs- in VII.46.1, but the Maruts are so called in V.52.13, 54.6.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYouthful (Maruts), approaching us with benevolent hearts, grant prosperity to those liberal men whoworship you, who zealously propitiate you, the showerers of rain, with oblations.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The Maruts of good drops who deserve (the soma-drink) and who go about practicing generosity all together.
With a better heart even than this [=usual generosity], o youths, turn yourselves hither toward us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Syntactic problems continue in this verse. Contra most interpr., I take ab as a continuation of vs. 17, still couched in the 3rd ps., and cd as a new clause directly addressing the Maruts in the 2nd ps. The first hemistich consists of two parallel relative clauses, with the two forms of y├й positioned at the extreme ends, opening and closing the half-verse. The clauses are connected by an inverse ca: #y├й ca тАж y├й#.

This inversion is phonologically motivated, producing a mirror image figure: #y├й c─Б╠Бrhanti тАж c├бranti y├й# (Saс╣Гhit─Б text, but 1st verb metrically to be read ca ├бrhanti).

There are further problems. ├бrhanti has no expressed object – unless mar├║taс╕е is taken as acc., with the subj. being unexpressed human worshipers; see OldenbergтАЩs reff.

This seems a thoroughly bad idea, given the rhetorical structure of this prag─Бtha. Geldner supplies тАЬzu heissenтАЭ (that is, тАЬdeserve [to be called]тАЭ), which seems a fairly radical addition; Renou тАЬnotre hommageтАЭ (so also Klein, DGRV I.186), which is somewhat easier to justify semantically but for which there is no parallel. My тАЬsoma drinkтАЭ is based on a number of passages where some expression containing p─лt├нm тАШdrinkтАЩ (+/- тАШsomaтАЩ) serves as obj. of тИЪarh (I.134.6, II.14.2, IV.47.2, V.51.6); this is the most common expressed obj. to тИЪarh.

In b m─лс╕╖h├║с╣гaс╕е is the problem. Technically speaking, this cannot be a nom. pl.

as I have rendered it. The correct form should be m─лс╕╖hv─Б╠Бс╣Гsaс╕е, which is found only once in the RV, though nearby (VIII.25.14, but not attributed to the same poet). Most take it here as the accusative pl. it appeas to be, referring to the generous (human) patrons whom the Maruts approach (e.g., Geldner тАЬund die zu den Lohnherrn insgesamt(?) kommenтАЭ). This is certainly possible, but, with Oldenberg, I nonetheless take it as a nominative, because the stem is often used of the Maruts, including in this very hymn (3c gen. pl. m─лс╕╖h├║с╣г─Бm). The misinterpretation could be aided by passages like VI.66.3 rudr├бsya y├й m─лс╕Нh├║с╣гaс╕е s├бnti putr─Б╠Бс╕е, where the adjective technically modifies gen. sg. Rudra, but could be interpr. as going with nom. pl. putr─Б╠Бс╕е. Cf. also VII.58.5, which is entirely ambiguous. It is indeed barely possible that m─лс╕╖h├║с╣гaс╕е here actually is a gen. sg., picking up the rudr├бsya of 17a, but I think this unlikely. The morphologically weak nom. pl. here might also be favored by phonological motivations, in order to produce a form similar to mar├║taс╕е in the previous p─Бda in the same metrical position (i.e., immediately preceding a four-syllable cadence).

y├║v─Бnaс╕е here is a voc.; the identical form in 17c is most likely a nominative.

The acc. to the same stem, y┼л╠Бnaс╕е, opens the next vs. (19a).

In d the Saс╣Гhit─Б vavс╣Ыdhvam must be read *vavс╣Ыd-dhu vam with both distraction and a heavy root syllable (тИЪvс╣Ыt тАШturnтАЩ). For a similar situation, see ├бcidhvam in VIII.7.2, which must be read *├бcid-dhu vam (тИЪcit).

+Griffith

Even for their sake, O Youthful Ones, with kindest heart take us to you to be your own.

+Geldner

Und welche die gabensch├╢nen Marut zu hei├Яen verdienen und die zu den Lohnherren insgesamt kommen, mit noch besserem Herzen als diese, wendet euch, ihr J├╝nglinge, uns zu!

+Grassmann

Die reich an Gaben selbst den Maruts kommen gleich, und zu den gn├дd’gen gehn im Chor, Von denen auch, o jugendliche, wendet euch mit holdem Herzen zu uns her.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPraise, Sobhari, (and attract here) by a new song the youthful purifying showerers, as (a plural ughman)repeatedly drags his oxen.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As a plural ughma: “as a plural ughman repeatedly drawing the furrows (praises oraddressed) of his oxen”

+Jamison Brereton

To the youths, to the bulls, the pure ones, sing with your newest hymn, o Sobhari,
like a plowman to his cows [/celebrating (the Maruts) like cows].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As was pointed out in the published introduction, p─Бda c contains a pun: the intens.

part. c├бrkс╣Ыс╣гat can belong straightforwardly to тИЪkс╣Ыс╣г тАШploughтАЩ, and in this reading the simile depicts a person engaged in ploughing singing or otherwise verbally encouraging his team, just as Sobhari sings to the Maruts. (In this case g─Б╠Бс╕е would probably be better rendered тАЬoxen.тАЭ) But it can also be secondarily associated with the root тИЪkс╣Э тАШcelebrate, praiseтАЩ, which has a curiously formed 3rd sg. -se medial intensive c├бrkс╣Ыс╣гe (3x), beside act. carkar-/carkir-. For purposes of word play a nonce stem c├бrkс╣Ыс╣г- could be extracted from the isolated c├бrkс╣Ыс╣гe. In this reading Sobhari is praising the Maruts like cows (see vs. 21); in other words this is a sort of reverse d─Бnastuti. That the Maruts are called bulls in p─Бda b simply adds to the play.

Note also the phonological echo in g─Б╠Бya g─Б╠Б(с╕е).

+Griffith

O Sobhari, with newest song sing out unto the youthful purifying Bulls,
Even as a plougher to his steers.

+Geldner

Die Jugendlichen besinge fein, o Sobhari, mit neuestem Loblied, die Bullen, die Lauteren, wie der Pfl├╝gende die Stiere ermuntert;

+Grassmann

Die jungen Stiere schreie an, o Sobhari, mit neustem Lied die flammenden, Wie sein Gespann der Pfl├╝gende.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPropitiate wiс╕е praise he Maruts, the senders of rain, the givers of plural asure, the liberal bestowers offood; who are ever victorious in combats, and like a boxer who has been challenged over his challengerс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bestowers of food: or, the most illustrious, su┼Ыravastam─Б, “who are ever victorious in combats and everchallengers, like a challenge-worthy boxer”

+Jamison Brereton

Those who are victorious like a fist-fighter, to be invoked in all contests, among (all) Hotars,
those, like lustrous bulls, receiving the most praisesтАФextol them with a hymn: the Maruts, yes!

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner plausibly explains the sg. h├бvyaс╕е as attraction to the number in the simile (sg. muс╣гс╣нih─Б╠Б). One might also add that h├бvya- is overwhelmingly nom. sg, and there are no masc. pl. forms attested. There seems no obvious reason for such a grammatical restriction, but it may have contributed to the somewhat anomalous form here.

All standard interpr. (including mine) take the simile in b to be vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зa┼Ы candr─Б╠Бn n├б тАЬlike lustrous bulls,тАЭ despite the displaced simile marker – in part presumably because тАЬlike lustrous/brilliant onesтАЭ doesnтАЩt make much sense as a simile. I have no explanation for the placement of n├б, nor do I understand why this needs to be a simile at all, since the Maruts are regularly called bulls without such marking (see nearby 19b, e.g., as well as 9-10, 12). Perhaps it indirectly continues the pun in the simile in 19c, which in turn is continued in vs. 21.

+Griffith

Who, like a celebrated boxer, overcome the challengers in every fight:
They who, like shining bulls, are most illustrious-honour those Maruts with thy song.

+Geldner

Die die ├Ьberlegenen sind, anzurufen und herauszufordern wie der Faustk├дmpfer in allen K├дmpfen von Seiten der Opferpriester und Herausforderer. Lobe doch die Marut mit Preisrede, die schimmernden Bullen gleichen, die Hochber├╝hmtesten!

+Grassmann

Die kr├дftig wie ein vielbegehrter Ringer sind bei allem Streit und Kampfgew├╝hl, Wie sehr ber├╝hmte, glanzbegabte Heldenschar, die Maruts ehre mit Gesang.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMaruts, who are of like wrath, offspring of the maternal cow (Pс╣Ы┼Ыni), related by a common origin, theyseverally spread through the quarters of the horizon.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Or, Maruts, alike in energy, your kindred, the cows,severally lick up the quarters of the horizon;

Gav─Бс╕е = sun’s rays

+Jamison Brereton

Cows also, likewise akin through common birth, o Maruts of equal spirit,
lick each otherтАЩs humps.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The cow imagery of vs. 19 (and implicitly 20) continues here. Geldner and Renou take this as a simile (тАЬlike cowsтАЭ), but this requires interpr. cid as a simile marker, a function for cid that I do not believe in. It is even less likely because the next verse begins with a parallel structure (m├бrta┼Ы cid), where the cid is definitely not a simile marker. I do, however, think that the Maruts are identified with the cows here. There are several themes intertwined. The most obvious point of comparison between cows and Maruts is their common birth (saj─Бty├иna тАж s├бbandhavaс╕е) as a herd/flock and consequent lack of individual differentiation, a characteristic of the Maruts treated earlier, in vss. 13-14. But the Maruts also have a cow for a mother; this was asserted in 8c, and the phraseology there (g├│bandhavaс╕е suj─Бt─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАЬakin to a cow, well-bornтАЭ) is echoed here (g─Б╠Бvaс╕е тАж saj─Бty├иna тАж s├бbandhavaс╕е), thus alluding to the MarutsтАЩ kinship with cows. Hence s├бbandhu- here has two senses: both cows and Maruts have common birth within their own group (that is, cows with cows, Maruts with Maruts), but cows and Maruts have a common birth with each other (cows with Maruts, due to the MarutsтАЩ bovine mother). This type of kinship is treated also in 22ab. I also identified a secondary meaning in 8c: being akin to cows is a way of saying that the Maruts have cows to give, and I think that is slightly hinted at here.

I donтАЩt quite understand the relevance of тАЬthey lick each otherтАЩs humps.тАЭ L├╝ders (Varuс╣Зa 90) suggests that the vs. praises the unity (Eintract) of the Maruts, and, if somewhat sharpened, this may be the correct explanation. тАЬLick each otherтАЩs humpsтАЭ may be the equivalent of English тАЬwatch each otherтАЩs backsтАЭ: individuals act reciprocally (mith├бс╕е here) and protectively for the common good of the group.

Note the echo of the final words in a and b: тАж samanyavaс╕е# тАж s├бbandhavaс╕е#. The opening g─Б╠Бva┼Ы cid gh─Б also faintly echoes g─Б╠Бya g─Б╠Бopening 21a.

Die Rinder auch, die euch verwandt, durch gleichen Ursprung, gleichgesinnte Maruts, sind, Belecken ihre K├╢pfe sich.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMaruts, dancing (through the air), decorated with golden breast-plural tes, the mortal (who worships you)attains your brotherhood; speak favourably to us, for your affinity is ever (made known) at the regulated(sacrifice).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The mortal also will draw near to brotherhood with you, you dancers with brilliants on your breasts.
Take note of us, Maruts, for your firmly founded friendship exists always.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The theme of cross-species kinship in vs. 21 continues here, with the mortal seeking brotherhood (bhr─Бtс╣Ыtv├бm) with the Maruts.

The verse as a whole, balancing brotherhood (bhr─Бtс╣Ыtv├бm) and friendship (─Бptiv├бm), should be evaluated in conjunction with vs. 13 of the next hymn (VIII.21, by the same poet) abhr─Бtrvy╠е ├│ an─Б╠Бtv├бm, ├бn─Бpir indra jan├║с╣г─Б san─Б╠Бd asi / yudh├йd ─Бpitv├бm ichase, where Indra is said to lack either. See comm. thereon.

+Griffith

Even mortal man, ye Dancers breast adorned with gold, attains to brotherhood with you.
Mark ye and notice us, O Maruts; evermore your friendship is secured to us.

+Geldner

Selbst der Sterbliche soll eure Bruderschaft erlangen, ihr T├дnzer mit goldge-schm├╝ckter Brust. Gedenket unser, o Marut, denn immer ist eure Freundschaft zuverl├дssig!

+Grassmann

Der Sterbliche, o goldgeschm├╝ckte T├дnzer, geht euch an um eure Br├╝derschaft, O kommt zu uns, o Maruts her; denn stets verbleibt das Freundschaftsband, das uns vereint.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the relatively elementary figure in c m├бyo (no) bh┼лta тАж mayobhuvaс╕е.

The voc. asacadviс╣гaс╕е has given rise to multiple competing analyses, well summarized by Scarlatta in his detailed treatment of this hapax (246-48). Most start with dviс╣г- тАШhatred, haterтАЩ as 2nd member and some form of тИЪsac тАШfollow, accompanyтАЩ as its first, governing the second. The problem is what form of тИЪsac? It cannot be a straighforward thematic verbal stem or participle/injunctive (saca- or sacat- [though

*asacad-dviс╣гaс╕е is a phonologically possible underlying form]) because the Class I pres. of тИЪsac is resolutely middle. (Debrunner [Nachtr. AiG II.1.87] also disputes this analysis on the basis that the accent is wrong for a verbal governing cmpd of that sort, but since the form is a voc. and unaccented, this argument is inapplicable. [It does apply to the other form he mentions, jaradv├нс╣г-, but these forms do not have to be parallel.]) It is also possible to take it as a standard type of root noun cmpd with the root noun governing the 1st member (тАШhating the asacaтАЩ or тАШnot hating the sacaтАЩ; at some point I toyed with the idea of тАШhating the non-alignedтАЩ), but this still founders on the puzzle of asaca-. ScarlattaтАЩs own solution is to divide the cmpd differently, as asacad-v├нс╣г-, with тИЪviс╣г тАШbring aboutтАЩ as 2nd member and a form of тИЪsac (2) тАШdry outтАЩ as 1st member, hence тАШnot bringing about droughtтАЩ or тАШbringing about non-droughtтАЩ.

Unfortunately getting -sacat- from this root requires a lot of not too plausible machinery – it is no more straightforward than deriving -saca(t)- from тИЪsac (1) – though I am sympathetic to his argument that the meaning would fit well with the MarutsтАЩ character. My own тАШwho do not partner hatredтАЩ rests essentially on a loose interpr. of the verbal governing analysis presented first above, though I hold no particular brief for it. I would point out that if it does contain тИЪsac тАШaccompanyтАЩ, it could pair contrastively with sakh─Бyaс╕е in the preceding vs. (23c). A very weak argument for тИЪsac (1) and тИЪdviс╣г could be constructed on the basis of VIII.22.2, a hymn to the A┼Ыvins but also composed by Sobhari. There the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot is described as sacan─Б╠Бvantam тАШprovided with companionsтАЩ vel sim., the first word of p─Бda c, and as v├нdveс╣гasam тАШfree of hatredтАЩ, the first word of p─Бda d, with the same two roots. But I would not make much of this.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDo you, beholding every sort, collect them for (the good of) our bodies, ad instrumental uct us in their (uses); letthe cure of sickness (be the portion), Maruts, of him among us who for his wickedness is sick; re-establish hisenfeebled (frame).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Seeing it, you carry it all on your bodies. With it intercede for us. To ground (should go) the malady of the afflicted; make what has gone awry right again.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. marutaс╕е in c was carelessly omitted in the published translation

+Griffith

Ye carry on your bodies, ye who see it all: so bless us graciously therewith.
Cast, Maruts, to the ground our sick man’s malady: replace the dislocated limb.

+Geldner

All das ersp├дhend bringet ihr an euren Leibern mit; mit dem segnet uns! Zu Boden gehe das Gebreste unserer Kranken, ihr Marut! Bringet alles, was verrenkt ist, wieder zurecht!

+Grassmann

Die f├╝hrt allschauend alle unsern Leibern zu, mit denen schafft Erquickung uns; Zu Boden sinke unsres Kranken Siechthum auch, o Maruts, heilt, was schadhaft ist.

+Elizarenkova
